# 159\n
{London, British Library, Add. 23986 verso of roll: Interludium de Clerico et Puella}\n
ca1300\n
482 402 E\n
{=NW Lincs=}\n
{=Sample represents all the text in English in this hand=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The MS is a narrow roll of parchment with the dramatic verse interlude\n
written on one side of it. It finishes imperfectly. There is almost no\n
punctuation. The verses are broken up by the insertion of the relevant\n
speaker\'s name, sometimes boxed in ink lines, in the right hand\n
margin. In each case, an ink line runs between the lines of text to\n
the left margin to indicate precisely where the speaker changes=}\n
{=Script - early Anglicana with some influence from contemporary\n
documentary script=}\n
{=The first quarter of this side of the roll is blank except for modern\n
reference numbers and notes and some later medieval pen trials=} \n
{(*HIC *INCIPi^T *INTerLUDIUm DE CLerIcO & PUELLA(}\n

# 291\n
{London, British Library, Arundel 57, fols. 2r-4r; 13r-96v: Ayenbite of Inwyt, Pater Noster etc.}\n
C14a2\n
615 158 N\n
{=Canterbury, Kent=}\n
{=Sample tagged: fols. 2r-4r, 13r-32v, 79v-81v, 91r-96v=}\n
{=Script - according to Gradon (1979:7), quoting Malcolm Parkes: "the\n
script represents an idiosyncratic variant of the earlier engrossing\n
hand and marks a stage towards later Anglicana Formata"=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The Ayenbite of Inwyt is a translation of the Somme le Roi of 1280.\n
Most of the MS, fols. 13r-96v, is in the hand of Dan Michel, and was\n
written in 1340 at St Augustine\'s Canterbury - see, in Dan Michel\'s\n
own hand, the colophon on fol. 94r and the statement on fol. 2r. By\n
this date Dan Michel was an old man of 70 years or more, the language\n
may therefore be taken as representative of the late 13th rather than\n
the mid-14th. The first quire, fols 1-12, was added later and consists\n
of a copy of Aristotle\'s De Anima, see Pamela Gradon\'s notes - EETS OS\n
278, 1979 - to her reissue of Morris\'s 1866 edn - EETS OS 23. The\n
author`s preface and table of contents, are written by Dan Michel on\n
the bottoms of fols. 2r-4r of this first quire. Neither the Latin of\n
the Aristotle text, nor various prophecies, also in Latin and in a\n
later hand, are recorded here. After the Ayenbite proper follow in\n
English, also in DM\'s hand, Pater Noster, Ave Maria and Creed (fol. 94r);\n
Pseudo-Anselm De Custodia Interioris Hominis (fols. 94v-96v); and two\n
more versions of Ave Maria (fol. 96v). Dan Michel uses punctus, punctus\n
elevatus, virgule, colon, punctus interrogativus and paraph. These\n
are recorded as . .\' , : ? and para respectively. DM also uses a\n
marginal obelus to draw attention to points of interest. It is the\n
form of three dots in a triangle with a vertical line beneath=}\n
{=Original transcript provided by JJS, corrected, annotated and tagged\n
from microfilm by ML=}\n
{~f2r~}\n
{para}\n

!_*C:*C:\n
{=For the next four lines of text, the left hand part of the\n
page is taken up by the letters :*M^I:*C:*C: written very large.\n
Each colon represents three punctus one above the other in the MS.\n

{=sic - Morris (1866) reads YDIFT and emends to YDIzT. Gradon (1979)\n
accepts Morris\'s reading and suggests YDIFT may be an early example of\n
the change from xt to ft, referring to Jordan paras 196 n. and 294.\n
But here DM definitely writes ST not FT. With ST the ascenders are\n
habitually ligatured as is the case here, whilst they are not so\n
joined in FT. The ST spelling here for xt must therefore represent\n
the 13th-century usage, more commonly seen in SWML texts, and\n
apparently adopted from Anglo-French=}\n
